Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The equation C=75h+125 gives the amount a electrician charges for a job that takes h hours.
  - The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job.
 
To solve this problem, we need to first find the amount Mr. Roland was charged by the electrician, then use that to find how much Ms. Sanchez was charged.
Let's represent the amount Mr. Roland was charged by R, and the amount Ms. Sanchez was charged by S. Then, we can set up the following equations: 

$$R = 75h + 125$$

$$S = 75(h+2) + 125$$

The first equation is obtained by plugging in h hours for Mr. Roland's job, while the second equation is for Ms. Sanchez's job (where h+2 is used because the electrician worked 2 hours longer).

Now, we need to find the difference between S and R:

$$S - R = 75(h+2) + 125 - (75h + 125)$$
$$S - R = 75h + 150 - 75h$$
$$S - R = 150$$

Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$150$ more than Mr. Roland.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
Given the equation $C=75h+125$. We need to find the difference between the amounts charged to Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland when the number of hours worked on Ms. Sanchez's job is 2 more than the hours worked on Mr. Roland's job.
Let the number of hours worked on Mr. Roland's job be $t$.
Then the number of hours worked on Ms. Sanchez's job is $t+2$.
Substituting $t$ and $t+2$ into the equation $C=75h+125$ gives the amounts charged to Mr. Roland and Ms. Sanchez respectively. 
Action: Answer("C")  
Solving for the difference in the amounts,   
\begin{align*}
\text{Difference} &= \text{Amount Charged to Ms. Sanchez} - \text{Amount Charged to Mr. Roland}\\
&= [(75)(t+2) + 125] - [(75)(t) + 125]\\
&= 75 \cdot 2\\
&= 150
\end{align*}
Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$150$ more than he charged Mr. Roland. Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ \$ 150}$.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  If the electrician worked for $h$ hours, the amount he charged is $C = 75h + 125$ dollars.
  Ms. Sanchez's job took 2 hours longer than Mr. Roland's job.
  To find the difference between the amounts charged for Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland's job, we need to subtract the amounts, i.e., $C_{\text{Sanchez}} - C_{\text{Roland}}$.
  To find the amount charged for Sanchez's job, we need to know how many hours the electrician worked for her.
  To find the amount charged for Roland's job, we also need to know how many hours the electrician worked for him.
  We can use algebra to solve the problem.

Action: 
Let $h_R$ be the number of hours the electrician worked for Mr. Roland, then Ms. Sanchez's job took $h_R + 2$ hours. Therefore,
- The amount charged for Mr. Roland's job is $C_R = 75h_R + 125$ dollars.
- The amount charged for Ms. Sanchez's job is $C_S = 75(h_R + 2) + 125 = 75h_R + 275$ dollars.

The difference in the amounts charged is:
$$C_S - C_R = (75h_R + 275) - (75h_R + 125) = 150$$

Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$ 150$ more than Mr. Roland. The answer is (C).
Response 3:
Knowledge:
The electrician charges $C = 75h + 125$ dollars for a job that takes $h$ hours.
Action: 

Let's call the number of hours the electrician worked on Mr. Roland's job as $x$ hours. 

Then we know the electrician worked $(x+2)$ hours on Ms. Sanchez's job. 

Therefore, the cost of doing the job for Mr. Roland is $C_R = 75x + 125$ dollars. 

The cost of doing the job for Ms. Sanchez is $C_S = 75(x+2) + 125 = 75x + 175$ dollars. 

Finally, we can calculate the difference in cost between the two jobs by subtracting $C_R$ from $C_S$: 

\begin{align*}
C_S - C_R &= (75x + 175) - (75x + 125) \\
&= 50 \\
\end{align*}

So the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$50$ more than Mr. Roland for the job.

Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The energy per gram of protein is 4 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules.
  The energy per gram of fat is 9 food calories or 37.7 kilojoules.
  The energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules.
  
To find the expression for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$, we need to first set up an equation representing the total amount of energy in the granola bar:
$4p + 9f + 4c = 180$ 

Then, we isolate the term $f$ and simplify using algebra:
$9f = 180 - 4p - 4c$
$f = \frac{180 - 4p - 4c}{9}$
$f = \frac{20(9) - 4p - 4c}{9}$
$f = \frac{20(4) + 20(5) - 4p - 4c}{9}$
$f = \frac{4(5+p+c)}{9} + \frac{20}{9}$

Simplified, this expression becomes:
$f = \frac{4}{9}(p+c) + \frac{20}{9}$

The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market at the equilibrium price. 
  To find the equilibrium price, we need to find the price that makes the quantity supplied exactly match the quantity demanded.
  $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
  $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Action: 
  At equilibrium, the quantity demanded equals the quantity supplied. Therefore, we need to solve the equation $S(P) = D(P)$ to find the equilibrium price. 
  
  Substituting $S(P)$ and $D(P)$ from the given functions, we get:
  
  $\frac{1}{2} P + 40 = 220 - P$
  
  Solving for $P$, we get:
  
  $P = 180$
  
  Therefore, the equilibrium price is $\$180$, which is not among the answer choices. To choose the best answer, we need to find the closest price among the answer choices to the equilibrium price.

  $D(P)=220-P$ represents the quantity demanded as a function of the price.

  To solve for variable $x$ in a fraction, we can cross-multiply the fractions. That is, we can multiply the numerator of one fraction by the denominator of the other fraction. Then we set the resulting equations equal to each other and solve for the variable.

Action: 
First, we cross-multiply, to get: 

  $5(x+20) = 15x$

Distribute $5$ on the left side:

  $5x + 100 = 15x$

Subtract $5x$ from both sides:

  $100 = 10x$

Finally, we solve for $\frac{x}{5}$:

  $\frac{x}{5}=\frac{1}{2}$

Thus, the answer is  D: $\frac{1}{2}$

Topic: Math
Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 7
  C: 16
  D: 79
Response 0:
Knowledge: To solve for k, we can isolate the variable k by squaring both sides of the equation, then simplify and solve for k.

$$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$

$$(\sqrt{k+2}-x)^2=0^2$$

$$k+2-2x\sqrt{k+2}+x^2=0$$

$$k+2-x^2=2x\sqrt{k+2}$$

$$(k+2-x^2)^2=(2x\sqrt{k+2})^2$$

Action: Answer("C") 

Substituting $x = 9$:

$$(k+2-9^2)^2=(2\cdot9\sqrt{k+2})^2$$
$$(k-79)^2=36(k+2)$$
$$k^2-158k+6241=36k+72$$
$$k^2-194k+6169=0$$

Using the quadratic formula:

$$k = \frac{194 \pm \sqrt{194^2 - 4\cdot1\cdot6169}}{2\cdot1}$$

$$k = \frac{194 \pm \sqrt{37636 - 24676}}{2}$$

$$k = \frac{194 \pm \sqrt{12960}}{2}$$

$$k = \frac{194 \pm 120}{2}$$

$$k = 157, 37$$

Since we are looking for the value of $k$ in this particular equation, $k$ cannot be negative. Therefore, $k=16$ is the correct answer.

Action:

&\sqrt{k+2}-x=0\\
\implies &(\sqrt{k+2}-x)^2=0^2\\

\implies &k+2=x(2\sqrt{k+2}-x)\\

\implies &4(k+2)=81^2\\
\implies &4(k+2)=6561\\
\implies &k+2=1640.25\\
\implies &k=1638.25\\
\end{align*}

$-52=1.08 t$

  a&=1,052+1.08 t \\
  1.08 t &= a - 1,052 \\
  t &= \frac{a - 1,052}{1.08}
  \end{aligned}
  $$
  We want to find the value of $t$ that makes $a$ closest to 1,000. Since 1,000 is between 1,052 and 1,080, we know that $t$ must be negative (since $1.08t$ must be negative to get to 1,000). We can approximate the value of $t$ that gives $a \approx 1,000$ using the choices:
  Plugging the temperature into the equation we have:
  $$
  \begin{aligned}
  t &= \frac{a - 1,052}{1.08}\\
  t_1 &= \frac{1,000 - 1,052}{1.08} \approx -48.15 \approx \boxed{\mathrm{(B)}}
  \end{aligned}
  $$

  - To find the temperature that will be closest to 1000 feet per second, we need to solve for $t$ such that $|a - 1000|$ is minimized.

  The closest temperature to $-48.15^{\circ}F$ from the list is $-48^{\circ}F$

Topic: Math
Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To solve the equation, one needs to simplify it and then collect like terms. This can be done as follows:
  \begin{align*}
  2ax-15&=3(x+5)+5(x-1) \\
  2ax-15&=3x+15+5x-5\\
  2ax-15&=8x+10
  \end{align*}
  Moving all the $x$ terms to one side and all the constants to the other side, we get:
  \begin{align*}
  2ax-8x&=25\\
  (2a-8)x&=25
  \end{align*}
  The equation has no solutions if the coefficient of $x$ on the left-hand side is nonzero and the right-hand side is nonzero. In this case, the right-hand side is nonzero (equal to 25), so the coefficient of $x$ on the left-hand side (which is $2a-8$) must be zero. Solving for $a$, we get:
  \begin{align*}
  2a-8&=0\\
  2a&=8\\
  a&=4
  \end{align*}
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
First, we simplify the equation:
$$2ax-15=3x+15+5x-5.$$ Simplifying the right-hand side: $$2ax-15=8x+10.$$ And: $$2ax=8x+25.$$ Dividing by $x$ (noting that $x$ cannot be $0$ as that would make the left-hand side undefined), we have $$2a=8+\frac{25}{x}.$$ Since there is no value of $x$ that satisfies the original equation, there can be no value of $x$ that makes the right-hand side equal to $0$. Therefore, $x$ must approach $0$ from either the positive or negative direction. For $x$ arbitrarily close to $0^+$, $$\frac{25}{x}$$ will be extremely large and positive, so we can conclude that $$2a=8+\infty.$$ For $x$ arbitrarily close to $0^-$, $$\frac{25}{x}$$ will be extremely large and negative, so we can conclude that $$2a=8-\infty.$$ In either case, we can conclude that $$a=\frac{8}{2}=\boxed{\textbf{(B) } 4}.$$
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  To solve the equation, we will have to simplify it and then solve for $x$.
  If the equation has no solution, then it means the equations on both sides of the equal sign are not equal for any value of $x$.
  This can happen when the coefficients of $x$ on both sides of the equal sign are equal, but the constants are not equal. 

Action:

To make the coefficients of $x$ equal on both sides, we can simplify the right-hand side of the equation:
$$2ax - 15 = 3(x + 5) + 5(x - 1)$$
$$2ax - 15 = 3x + 15 + 5x - 5$$
$$2ax - 15 = 8x + 10$$
$$(2a - 8)x = 25$$

Now, for the equation to have no solution, we need the coefficient of $x$ to be non-zero (otherwise, the equation simplifies to $0=25$ which has no solution), but the constants on both sides of the equal sign to be different.

The coefficient of $x$ is $2a - 8$ and we need it to be non-zero, so we can solve the equation $2a-8=0$ to find $a$:
$$2a - 8 = 0$$
$$2a = 8$$
$$a = 4$$

This means that if $a=4$, then the equation simplifies to $(2a-8)x=25$ which has no solution for $x$. Therefore, the answer is:

Topic: Math
Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
The $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the parabola defined by the function $f(x)=a(x-h)^2+k$ is $h$.

To find the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the parabola defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$, we need to use the formula $x=\frac{-b}{2a}$, where $a$ and $b$ are the coefficients of the quadratic function $f$.

Action: 
We can see that $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$. 
Therefore, $a=1$ and $b=4$. 
Plugging these values into the formula $x=\frac{-b}{2a}$, we get $x=\frac{-4}{2(1)}=-2$.
This means that the vertex of the parabola defined by $f$ has an $x$-coordinate of $-2$.
To find the interval containing $-2$, we need to look for the interval that contains $-2$. 
The only interval containing $-2$ is $-3<x<1$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The vertex of a parabola in the form $f(x)=a(x-h)^2+k$ has coordinates $(h,k)$.

To find the coordinates of the vertex of the function $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$, we first expand it to $f(x) = x^2 + 4x + 3$. Then, we can complete the square as follows:

\begin{align*}
f(x) &= x^2 + 4x + 3 \\
&= (x^2 + 4x + 4) - 1 \\
&= (x+2)^2 - 1
\end{align*}

So, the vertex of the parabolic graph of $f$ has coordinates $(-2,-1)$.

The $x$-coordinate of the vertex is $-2$. We want to find an interval that contains $-2$.

  The vertex of the graph of $f$ is at the point $(-2, f(-2)) = (-2, -1)$.

Question: $$\frac{2}{3}(9 x-6)-4=9 x-6$$Based on the equation above, what is the value of $3 x-2$ ?

  C: $-\frac{2}{3}$

$$\frac{2}{3}(9 x-6)-4=9 x-6$$ can be simplified as:
\begin{align*}
6x-4 -4 &= 9x-6 \times \frac{3}{2} \\
6x-8 &= 9x-9 \\
-3x &= -1 \\
x &= \frac{1}{3}
\end{align*}

Using $x=\frac{1}{3}$, we can solve for $3x-2$:
\begin{align*}
3x-2 &= 3\times \frac{1}{3}-2 \\
&= 1-2 \\
&= -1
\end{align*}

Thus, the answer is **(A) -4**.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$Clayton will mix $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ by mass saline solution with $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ by mass saline solution in order to create an $18 \%$ by mass saline solution. The equation above represents this situation. If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution must he use?
Choices:
  A: 5
  B: 25
  C: 50
  D: 100
Response 0:
Knowledge:
The equation in the question is a linear equation with 2 variables. 
To solve the equation, we can simplify each side and combine like terms.
$\begin{aligned} 0.10x+0.20y&=0.18(x+y) \\ 0.10x+0.20y&=0.18x+0.18y \\ 0.02y&=0.08x \\ y&=4x \end{aligned}$
The question asks us to find the value of $x$.

Action: 
Since Clayton uses $100$ milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, we know that $y=100$.
Substitute this into the equation we found earlier: $\begin{aligned} y&=4x \\ 100&=4x \\ 25&=x \end{aligned}$
Therefore, Clayton must use $25$ milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution. Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ 25}$.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  In a solution of $m$ grams of mass, the percent concentration by mass is given by $\frac{mass \; of \; solute}{m} \cdot 100$.
Action: 
  First, we need to find $x+y$, the total volume of the saline solution that Clayton will create.
  We can solve the given equation for $x+y$ as follows:
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18 x+0.18 y$$
  $$0.02 y=0.08 x$$
  $$y=4x$$
  Also, we are given that $y=100$, so $x=25$. 
  Therefore, Clayton needs to use $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ 25}$ milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The equation $0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$ represents the fact that the total amount of saline in $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ saline solution plus the total amount of saline in $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ saline solution is equal to the total amount of saline in the resulting $(x+y)$ milliliters of $18 \%$ saline solution.
  
Let $x$ be the number of milliliters of $10 \%$ solution that Clayton needs to use. Then, he must use $100$ milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution. We can plug these values into the equation above and solve for $x$.
$$0.10 x+0.20 (100)=0.18(x+100)$$
$$0.10 x+20=0.18x+18$$
$$0.08 x=2$$
$$x=25$$
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  - In a mixture, the amount of solute is the sum of the amounts of solute in each component.
  - The mass percentage of a solution is equal to the mass of solute divided by the mass of the solution times 100%.
  - We can use the equation given to find the value of x.
  
Solution:
Let x be the amount of $10 \%$ by mass solution that Clayton will use. Since Clayton uses 100 milliliters of $20 \%$ by mass solution, then $y = 100 \text{ ml}$. We can use the given equation to solve for $x$:
$$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
Substituting $y = 100$ and simplifying:
$$0.1 x + 0.2(100) = 0.18(x + 100)$$
$$0.1 x + 20 = 0.18x + 18$$
$$0.02x = 2$$
$$x = 100$$
Therefore, Clayton must use 100 milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution.

We also know that the mass of saline in the mixture is $(v/10)\times 10 + (100/100)\times 20$ grams (the first term is the mass of saline in $v$ milliliters of $10 \%$ solution, and the second term is the mass of saline in $100$ milliliters of $20 \%$ solution.   $$\frac{(v/10)\times 10 + (100/100)\times 20}{v+100} = 0.18$$
  $$\frac{v}{v+100} = 0.2$$
  $$v = 25$$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What are the solutions to $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0 ?$
Choices:
  A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  B: $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{30}}{3}$
  C: $x=-6 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  D: $x=-6 \pm 6 \sqrt{2}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can use the quadratic formula to find the solutions to a quadratic equation of the form $ax^2 + bx + c = 0.$
  The quadratic formula for finding the solutions of $ax^2 + bx + c = 0$ is given by $x=\frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^{2}-4 a c}}{2 a}.$

Action: 
  Comparing $ax^2 + bx + c = 0$ with $3 x^{2}+12x+6=0$ tells us that $a = 3, b = 12,$ and $c = 6.$
  Substituting the values of $a$, $b$, and $c$ in the quadratic formula, we have $x = \frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{12^{2}-4(3)(6)}}{2(3)}.$
  Simplifying the expression gives $x = \frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{96}}{6}.$
  Further simplification gives $x = -2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{24}}{6},$ which is equal to $x = -2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{4}}{1} \sqrt{6}.$
  Therefore, the solutions to the equation $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0$ are $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{6}.$
  Answer: Answer("B")

Question: In planning maintenance for a city's infrastructure, a civil engineer estimates that, starting from the present, the population of the city will decrease by 10 percent every 20 years. If the present population of the city is 50,000, which of the following expressions represents the engineer's estimate of the population of the city $t$ years from now?
Choices:
  A: $50,000(0.1)^{20 t}$
  B: $50,000(0.1)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
  C: $50,000(0.9)^{20 t}$
  D: $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The city's population will decrease by 10 percent every 20 years.
  - The present population of the city is 50,000.
  
To solve this problem, we need to find an expression that gives us the population of the city t years from now. Let's break down the problem into parts:

1. Every 20 years, the population will decrease by 10 percent. 
2. To find the population after 20 years, we need to calculate 50,000 - 0.1 * 50,000 = 45,000. 
3. To find the population after 40 years, we need to calculate 45,000 - 0.1 * 45,000 = 40,500. 
4. To find the population after 60 years, we need to calculate 40,500 - 0.1 * 40,500 = 36,450.

Notice that after 20 years, the population will be 45,000, which is 0.9 times the present population. After 40 years, the population will be 40,500, which is 0.9 times the population after 20 years. This pattern continues every 20 years, so we can write an expression that involves 0.9 raised to a power of t/20, where t is the number of years from now. We multiply by 50,000 because that is the present population.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If the population decreases by 10% every 20 years, that means that the population multiplies by 0.9 every 20 years (since 1 - 0.1 = 0.9).
  
Action:

Using the knowledge above, the expression should be of the form $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$ because the population decreases 10% (or multiplied by a factor of 0.9) for every 20 years. Thus, the answer is (D) $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$.

To solve this problem, we can use the formula for exponential decay, which is:

$y = a(1-r)^{t}$ 

where:
  y = the population after t years
  a = the initial population (present population = 50,000)
  r = the decay rate (10% or 0.1)
  t = time in years

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangle was altered by increasing its length by 10 percent and decreasing its width by $p$ percent. If these alterations decreased the area of the rectangle by 12 percent, what is the value of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 22
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
Let the original length be $l$ and the original width be $w$.
The original area is $l \cdot w$.
After increasing the length by 10%, the new length is $1.1l$.
After decreasing the width by $p$%, the new width is $(1-\frac{p}{100})w$.
The new area is $(1-0.12)l \cdot (1-\frac{p}{100})w$. 

Solve for $p$ in the equation $(1-0.12)l \cdot (1-\frac{p}{100})w = l \cdot w$.
$0.88(1-\frac{p}{100})=1$
$1-\frac{p}{100}=\frac{1}{0.88}$
$p=100(\frac{1}{0.88}-1)$
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
The area of a rectangle with length $l$ and width $w$ is $A = lw$.
If the length of a rectangle is increased by $x$ percent and its width is decreased by $y$ percent, then the new area is $A' = \frac{(100+x)}{100}l \cdot \frac{(100-y)}{100}w$.
If the new area is 12 percent less than the original area, then $A' = 0.88A$.

Let $l'$ and $w'$ be the new length and width, respectively.
We are given that $l' = \frac{(100+10)}{100}l = 1.1l$ and that $w' = \frac{(100-p)}{100}w$.
We are also given that $A' = 0.88A$.
Substituting these expressions into the expression for $A'$ and simplifying, we get:
$1.1lw\left(1-\frac{p}{100}\right) = 0.88lw$
Simplifying further, we get:
$p = \frac{22}{3} \approx 7.33$

  - The formula for the area of a rectangle is A = l * w, where l is length and w is width.

  - If we know the percent change of one dimension (length or width) and the percent change of the area, we can solve for the percent change of the other dimension.
  - The percent change of a dimension can be calculated using the formula: (new - old) / old * 100%

Let's begin by setting up the equation to represent the information given in the problem:
- A_a = (1 + 0.1) * l * (1 - p/100) * w
- We know that the altered area is 12% less than the original area, so we can set up the following equation:
- A_a = (1 - 0.12) * A_o

Let's simplify the equation for the altered area by substituting the expression for A_o:
- (1 + 0.1) * l * (1 - p/100) * w = (1 - 0.12) * (l * w)
- Distributing on the left side:
- l * w - 0.12 * l * w = (1.1l) * (1 - p/100) * w
- Factoring out l and w on both sides:
- l * w * (1 - 0.12) = l * w * (1.1 - 0.011p)
- Simplifying:
- 0.88lw = 1.089l * w * (1 - p/100)
- Dividing both sides by lw and multiplying by 100:
- 88 = 108.9 * (1 - p/100)
- Dividing both sides by 108.9:
- 0.808 = 1 - p/100
- Solving for p:
- p/100 = 0.192
- p = 19.2

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 79 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $(a x+2)(b x+7)=15 x^{2}+c x+14$ for all values of $x$, and $a+b=8$, what are the two possible values for $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3 and 5
  B: 6 and 35
  C: 10 and 21
  D: 31 and 41
Response 0:
Knowledge:
Expanding the left side of the equation yields:
$(a x+2)(b x+7)=abx^2 + (7a+2b)x+14$ 

The polynomial on the right is $15x^2 + cx+14$.

For these two polynomials to be equal, their coefficients must be equal.
In particular:
$ab=15$
$7a+2b=c$

$a+b=8$

To find the values of $a$ and $b$ which satisfy $a+b=8$ and $ab=15$ we can use the quadratic formula. 
$a, b = \dfrac{8 \pm \sqrt{8^2 - 4(1)(-15)}}{2(1)} = \dfrac{8 \pm \sqrt{244}}{2} = 4 \pm \sqrt{61}$

Now, we can calculate the two possible values of $c$ as:
$7a+2b = 7(4+\sqrt{61})+2(4-\sqrt{61}) = 42+5\sqrt{61}$ 
or 
$7a+2b = 7(4-\sqrt{61})+2(4+\sqrt{61}) = 42-5\sqrt{61}$.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: We can expand the left side of the given equation, then set the resulting polynomial equal to the given polynomial. Then we can match the coefficients of the terms with the same degree on both sides of the equation to get a system of equations in $a$, $b$, and $c$. Finally, we can solve for $c$ using the system of equations and the restriction $a+b=8$.

Solution:
Expanding the left side of the equation, we get
$$(a x+2)(b x+7)=a b x^{2}+(7 a+2 b) x+14.$$
Setting this equal to the given polynomial $15 x^{2}+c x+14$, we get the system of equations
$$\begin{aligned} a b &=15 \\ 7 a+2 b &=c \\ a+b &=8. \end{aligned}$$
From the first equation, we have $ab=15$ and, since $a$ and $b$ are both positive integers, the only possibilities are $(a,b)=(1,15)$ or $(a,b)=(3,5)$. Using the second equation, we can solve for $c$ using each pair of values for $a$ and $b$:
$$c=7a+2b=7(1)+2(15)=37$$
or
$$c=7a+2b=7(3)+2(5)=29.$$
Therefore, the two possible values of $c$ are 29 and 37.

Response 4:
To solve this problem, we need to first expand the left side of the equation, and then compare it to the right side. This gives us a system of equations that we can solve for $a$, $b$, and $c$. Once we know $a$ and $b$, we can find the two possible values of $c$.

Expanding the left side, we get:

$$
(a x+2)(b x+7) = a b x^2 + (7 a + 2 b) x + 14
$$

Comparing with the right side, we get:

$$
\begin{aligned}
a b &= 15 \\
7 a + 2 b &= c \\
14 &= 14
\end{aligned}
$$

We are given that $a + b = 8$, so we can solve for $a$ and $b$ as follows:

$$
\begin{aligned}
a + b &= 8 \\
b &= 8 - a
\end{aligned}
$$

Substituting into the equation for $a b$, we get:

$$
a (8 - a) = 15 \quad \Rightarrow \quad a^2 - 8 a + 15 = 0
$$

This quadratic equation factors as $(a - 3)(a - 5) = 0$, so the possible values for $a$ are $a = 3$ and $a = 5$. This gives us values for $b$ as well:

$$
\begin{aligned}
a = 3 &\quad \Rightarrow \quad b = 8 - a = 5 \\
a = 5 &\quad \Rightarrow \quad b = 8 - a = 3
\end{aligned}
$$

Finally, we can substitute these values into the equation for $c$:

$$
\begin{aligned}
7 a + 2 b &= c \\
a = 3, b = 5 &\quad \Rightarrow \quad c = 31 \\
a = 5, b = 3 &\quad \Rightarrow \quad c = 31
\end{aligned}
$$

So the two possible values for $c$ are $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}\ 31 \text{ and } 41}$.

Topic: Math
Question: What is the set of all solutions to the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x ?$
Choices:
  A: $\{-1,2\}$
  B: $\{-1\}$
  C: $\{2\}$
  D: There are no solutions to the given equation.
Response 0:
Knowledge:
To solve this equation, we need to remember a property of square roots: $\sqrt{x^2}=|x|.$ This means that, for any real number $x,$ we have $\sqrt{x^2}=|x|.$
Using this property and some algebraic manipulation, we can solve the equation as follows:
\begin{align*}
\sqrt{x+2}&=-x \\
|x|&=-x &\text{Since }\sqrt{x+2} \ge 0\\
x&=-x &\text{Since } x\le 0 \text{ due to the square root} \\
x&=0
\end{align*}
Checking our solution, we see that $\sqrt{0+2}=2.$ Since $-0=0,$ we see that $x=0$ is indeed a valid solution.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
To solve the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$, we first square both sides. This gives $x+2 = x^{2}$.
By subtracting $x$ and $2$ from both sides, we get $x^{2} - x -2 = 0$.
We can then factor the left hand side  to $(x-2)(x+1) = 0$.
So the solutions are given by $x-2=0$ or $x+1=0$.

A: $\{-1,2\}$ is not the correct answer as $\{-1\}$ is the only solution.
B: $\{-1\}$ is the correct answer.
C: $\{2\}$ is not the correct answer.
D: There are solutions to the given equation.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  For the square root of a real number to exist, it must be non-negative. This means that $x+2\ge 0.$ 
  Furthermore, the square root of any non-negative number is non-negative. 
  Therefore, $\sqrt{x+2}\ge 0.$ 
  Since $-x$ is either negative or zero, we must have 
  $$\sqrt{x+2}=-x\ge 0.$$ 
  This implies that $x\le 0.$ 

  Squaring both sides of $ \sqrt{x+2}=-x $, we have $x+2=x^2$. Rearranging, we have $x^2-x-2=0$, which factors as $(x-2)(x+1)=0.$ Hence, $x=2$ or $x=-1.$ 
  However, since we must have $x\le 0,$ the only solution is $x=-1.$

Response 6:
Knowledge: To solve the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$ first we need to isolate the square root expression on one side by squaring both sides of the equation. But, we have to check whether the solutions obtained from squaring both sides are valid or not, because squaring both sides can give us extraneous solutions.
$$\sqrt{x+2}=-x$$
Squaring both sides, we get
\begin{align*}
(\sqrt{x+2})^2&=(-x)^2\\
x+2 &=x^2\\
\Rightarrow x^2-x-2&=0
\end{align*}
Now, we can solve for x by factorizing the quadratic equation obtained above:
\begin{align*}
x^2-x-2&=0\\
\Rightarrow x^2-2x+x-2&=0\\
\Rightarrow x(x-2)+1(x-2)&=0\\
\Rightarrow (x-2)(x+1)&=0
\end{align*}
So, the solutions are $x=2$ or $x=-1$.

Checking the validity of the solutions, we can see that $x=2$ doesn't satisfy the original equation because $\sqrt{2+2}\neq -2$. So, the only solution to the equation is $x=-1$.

  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The linear equation is given by the form: $y = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The slope of the line between two points $(x_1, y_1)$ and $(x_2, y_2)$ is given by: $m = \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
  
Solution:
  We can use two points from the table to determine the slope of the line.
  For example, using the points ($128, 950$) and ($450, 3365$) we have: $m = \frac{3365-950}{450-128} = \frac{2415}{322} \approx 7.5$.
  The slope of the line is approximately 7.5, so options A, B, and C can be ruled out since they have a different slope.
  To find the y-intercept, we can use any of the points from the table and solve for b.
  Using the point ($128, 950$), we have: $950 = 7.5(0.128) + b \Rightarrow b \approx 855$.
  Therefore, the linear function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price is $r(p) = 7.5p + 855$, which corresponds to option D.

Topic: Math
Question: Nate walks 25 meters in 13.7 seconds. If he walks at this same rate, which of the following is closest to the distance he will walk in 4 minutes?
Choices:
  A: 150 meters
  B: 450 meters
  C: 700 meters
  D: 1,400 meters
Response 0:
Knowledge:
   - Nate walks 25 meters in 13.7 seconds which means his walking rate is 25/13.7 m/s.
   - 4 minutes is equal to 240 seconds.
   
Calculation:
   - Nate's walking rate = 25m/13.7s = 1.82 m/s.
   - Distance covered in 240 seconds = 1.82 m/s × 240 s = 436.8 ≈ 450
Choice:
   Nate will walk approximately 450 meters in 4 minutes. Therefore, the closest answer is option B. Answer("B").
Response 1:

  - To find the distance Nate will walk in 4 minutes, we need to know his speed in meters per second.
  - His speed in meters per second can be calculated by dividing the distance he walks by the time he takes: speed = distance ÷ time.

Calculation:
  - Nate's speed = 25 meters ÷ 13.7 seconds = 1.8251 meters per second.
  - Nate's distance in 4 minutes = speed × time = 1.8251 meters per second × 240 seconds = 438.024 meters.

Round-off:
  - The closest answer choice to 438.024 meters is B: 450 meters.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 87 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& b=2.35+0.25 x \\& c=1.75+0.40 x\end{aligned}$$In the equations above, $b$ and $c$ represent the price per pound, in dollars, of beef and chicken, respectively, $x$ weeks after July 1 during last summer. What was the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 2.60$
  B: $\$ 2.85$
  C: $\$ 2.95$
  D: $\$ 3.35$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
We are given two equations as follows:
$$b=2.35+0.25x$$
$$c=1.75+0.40x$$
We have to find the value of $b$ when $b=c$.
Action: 
When $b=c$, we can equate the two equations as follows:
$$2.35+0.25x = 1.75+0.40x$$
$$0.15x = 0.60$$
$$x = 4$$
So, after four weeks of July 1, the price per pound of beef and chicken were the same. Now, we can find the value of $b$ when $x=4$.
$$b=2.35+0.25(4)$$
$$b=2.35+1$$
$$b=3.35$$
Therefore, the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken was $\$ 3.35$. Hence, the answer is (D).
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
We need to find the value of $x$ when $b=c$. We can then substitute that value of $x$ in either equation to find the common value of $b$ and $c$.

Solution:
Since $b = 2.35 + 0.25x$ and $c = 1.75 + 0.40x$, we can equate them and solve for $x$ to find when the prices were equal:
$$ 2.35+0.25x=1.75+0.40x \implies 0.15x=0.60 \implies x=4 $$
So, the prices were equal 4 weeks after July 1. We can substitute $x=4$ in either equation to get the common price of beef and chicken:
$$ b = 2.35 + 0.25 \times 4 = 2.35 + 1.00 = \boxed{\$ 3.35} $$
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The problem asks to find the value of $b$ when $b=c$. 
  $b=2.35+0.25 x$ and $c=1.75+0.40 x$ are equations that relate $b$ and $c$ to $x$.
Action: 

Since $b=c$, we can set the two given equations equal to each other and solve for $x$:

$$0.15 x=0.6$$
$$x=4$$

$$b=2.35+0.25(4)$$
$$b=3.35$$

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D) } \$3.35}$.

  $$b=c.$$

\end{aligned}$$
When $x=4$ weeks, $b=c=2.35+0.25\cdot 4 = 2.35+1=3.35$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The first year Eleanor organized a fund-raising event, she invited 30 people. For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year. If $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event, which of the following statements best describes the function $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: The function $f$ is a decreasing linear function.
  B: The function $f$ is an increasing linear function.
  C: The function $f$ is a decreasing exponential function.
  D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  - For each subsequent year, she invited double the number of people as the previous year.
  - $f(n)$ represents the number of people invited $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event.
  
Analysis:
  - After 1 year, Eleanor invites $2\cdot30=60$ people.
  - After 2 years, Eleanor invites $2\cdot60=120$ people.
  - After 3 years, Eleanor invites $2\cdot120=240$ people.
  - After 4 years, Eleanor invites $2\cdot240=480$ people.
  - After 5 years, Eleanor invites $2\cdot480=960$ people.
  - We can express the number of people as an exponential function of the form $f(n)=30\cdot2^n$.
  - This means that as $n$ increases, $f(n)$ increases exponentially.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  In the first year Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year.
  
Analysis:
  2 * 30 = 60
  2 * 60 = 120
  2 * 120 = 240
  2 * 240 = 480
  2 * 480 = 960

  The function $f(n)$ is dependent on the number of years since the first year of the event, and at each year afterward, it follows an exponential pattern of growth in the number of attendees. Therefore, the best answer is D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.

Topic: Math
Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Let's focus on the relevant information: 
- $Never$: 31.3%
- $Rarely$: 24.3%
- $Often$: 13.5%
- $Always$: 30.9%

We need to find the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never." This means we can ignore the $31.3\%$ who answered "Never" when we calculate the probability. 

Let $A$ be the event that a tablet user answered "Always," and let $B$ be the event that a user did not answer "Never." We want to find $P(A|B)$.

Using Bayes' Theorem, we have:
$$P(A|B) = \frac{P(B|A)P(A)}{P(B)}$$

We know that:
- $P(A) = 0.309$ (from the table)
- $P(Never) = 0.313$ (from the table)
- $P(B) = 1 - P(Never) = 1 - 0.313 = 0.687$
- $P(B|A) = 1$ (since if a user answered "Always," then they did not answer "Never")

Plugging in these values, we get:
$$P(A|B) = \frac{1 \cdot 0.309}{0.687} \approx \boxed{\textbf{(B) }0.38}$$

Therefore, the closest probability to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never," is $\boxed{\textbf{(B) }0.38}$.

\begin{align*}
P(A| \text{not }N)&=\frac{P(\text{not }N|A)P(A)}{P(\text{not }N|A)P(A)+P(\text{not }N|\text{not }A)P(\text{not }A)} \\

&=\frac{0.213}{0.338} \\

\end{align*}

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& 2 x-3 y=-14 \\& 3 x-2 y=-6\end{aligned}$$If $(x, y)$ is a solution to the system of equations above, what is the value of $x-y$ ?

  A: -20
  B: $\quad-8$
  C: -4
  D: 8

- This system of equations can be solved using elimination or substitution method.
- To use elimination method, we can multiply the first equation by $-2$ and the second equation by $3$, then add the resulting equations. This will eliminate $x$ and allow us to solve for $y$. We can then substitute the value of $y$ back into one of the original equations to solve for $x$. Alternatively, we can solve for $x$ using elimination or substitution, and then solve for $y$ using the value of $x$.

- Multiply the first equation by $-2$: $$\begin{aligned} -4x + 6y &= 28 \\ 3x - 2y &= -6 \end{aligned} $$ 
- Multiply the second equation by $3$: $$\begin{aligned} 2x - 3y &= -14 \\ 9x - 6y &= -18 \end{aligned}$$ 
- Add the resulting equations: $$\begin{aligned} 5x &= 10 \\ x &= 2 \end{aligned}$$
- Substitute the value of $x$ into the second equation: $$\begin{aligned} 3(2) - 2y &= -6 \\ -2y &= -12 \\ y &= 6 \end{aligned}$$
- Calculate $x-y$: $$x-y=2-6=-4$$

\end{aligned}
$$
Therefore, the solution to the system of equations is $(x,y)=(2,-6)$. Thus, $x-y=2-(-6)=8$. 

Action: Answer("D")
Response 7:
To solve the system of equations using elimination method, we will need to multiply the first equation by 2 and the second equation by 3 so that the coefficients of $x$ in both equations become equal. This gives us the new system of equations:
$$\begin{aligned}& 4 x-6 y=-28 \\& 9 x-6 y=-18\end{aligned}$$
Next, we can subtract the second equation from the first equation to eliminate the $y$ terms:
$$-5x = -10$$
Solving for $x$, we get $x=2$. Substituting this value of $x$ in the first equation of the original system, we get $-3y=-10$, or $y=\frac{10}{3}$. Therefore, $x-y=2-\frac{10}{3}=\frac{4}{3}$.

Topic: Math
Question: A line in the $x y$-plane passes through the origin and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Which of the following points lies on the line?
Choices:
  A: $(0,7)$
  B: $(1,7)$
  C: $(7,7)$
  D: $(14,2)$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The slope-intercept form of the equation of a line is $y = mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the $y$-intercept of the line.
  
We know the line passes through the origin $(0,0)$ and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$, so its equation can be written as $y=\frac{1}{7}x$. 

We can now substitute each point to see which one satisfies the equation of the line:
  
  A: $(0,7)$ --> $y=\frac{1}{7}(0) = 0 \neq 7$
  B: $(1,7)$ --> $y=\frac{1}{7}(1) = \frac{1}{7} \neq 7$
  C: $(7,7)$ --> $y=\frac{1}{7}(7) = 1 \neq 7$
  D: $(14,2)$ --> $y=\frac{1}{7}(14) = 2$
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
    A line in the $x y$-plane can be defined by either: 
      - two points that the line passes through
      - point-slope form: $y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$, where $(x_1,y_1)$ is a point on the line and $m$ is the slope of the line. 
    The problem tells us that the line passes through the origin $(0,0)$ and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$.
    We can use the point-slope form $y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$ to find the equation of the line and then check which of the given points satisfy that equation.
    
Action: We know that the line passes through the origin $(0,0)$ and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Using the point-slope form of a line and plugging in $m=\frac{1}{7}$ and $(x_1,y_1)=(0,0)$, we get $y-0 = \frac{1}{7}(x-0)$. Simplifying, we get $y=\frac{1}{7}x$. We can now check which of the given points satisfy this equation:
  - A: $(0,7)$ does not satisfy the equation (when $x=0$, $y\neq7$)
  - B: $(1,7)$ does not satisfy the equation (when $x=1$, $y\neq1$)
  - C: $(7,7)$ satisfies the equation (when $x=7$, $y=1$)
  - D: $(14,2)$ does not satisfy the equation (when $x=14$, $y\neq2$)
Therefore, the point that lies on the line is (C) $(7,7)$.  
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The equation of a line in slope-intercept form is given by $y = mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  The line passes through the origin, so $b=0$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y = \frac{1}{7}x$.
  To check whether a point lies on the line, we can substitute its $x$ and $y$ coordinates into the equation of the line and see if the equation is true.
Action: Answer("A")  
Solution:
  The point $(0,7)$ has $x=0$ and $y=7$, so we substitute into the equation of the line:
  $$y = \frac{1}{7}x \quad\implies\quad 7 = \frac{1}{7}\cdot 0$$
  Since $7=0$ is not true, the point $(0,7)$ does not lie on the line.
  
  The point $(1,7)$ has $x=1$ and $y=7$, so we substitute into the equation of the line:
  $$y = \frac{1}{7}x \quad\implies\quad 7 = \frac{1}{7}\cdot 1$$
  Since $7=\frac{1}{7}$ is true, the point $(1,7)$ lies on the line.
  
  The point $(7,7)$ has $x=7$ and $y=7$, so we substitute into the equation of the line:
  $$y = \frac{1}{7}x \quad\implies\quad 7 = \frac{1}{7}\cdot 7$$
  Since $7=1$ is true, the point $(7,7)$ lies on the line.
  
  The point $(14,2)$ has $x=14$ and $y=2$, so we substitute into the equation of the line:
  $$y = \frac{1}{7}x \quad\implies\quad 2 = \frac{1}{7}\cdot 14$$
  Since $2=2$ is true, the point $(14,2)$ lies on the line.
  
  Therefore, the points that lie on the line are $(1,7)$, $(7,7)$, and $(14,2)$. Only option A is not a valid point that lies on the line. Answer("A").

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Jennifer bought a box of Crunchy Grain cereal. The nutrition facts on the box state that a serving size of the cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat. In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- One serving of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat.
- Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
- Jennifer's mixture of Crunchy Grain cereal and Super Grain cereal provides 270 calories per cup.
- Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup.

Let's denote the amount of Super Grain cereal Jennifer uses with $x$ cups.
Then the amount of Crunchy Grain cereal Jennifer uses is $(1-x)$ cups. 

To calculate the number of calories from Crunchy Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture, we can use the fact that a serving size is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories: 

- $\frac{3}{4}$ cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 210 calories
- $1$ cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides $\frac{4}{3} \cdot 210 \approx 280$ calories
- $(1-x)$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal provide $(1-x) \cdot 280$ calories

To calculate the number of calories from Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture, we can use the fact that the total number of calories in one cup of the mixture is 270:

- One cup of the mixture provides 270 calories
- $(1-x)$ cups of the mixture provide $(1-x) \cdot 210$ calories from Crunchy Grain cereal
- $x$ cups of the mixture provide $240x$ calories from Super Grain cereal
- So we have the equation: $(1-x) \cdot 280 + 240x = 270$
- Solving for x gives: $x = \frac{1}{3}$

Therefore, Jennifer uses $\frac{1}{3}$ cup of Super Grain cereal.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  One serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat.
  One serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is 5% of the daily allowance for adults.
  Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup.
  Jennifer's mixture of Crunchy Grain cereal and Super Grain cereal has a total of 270 calories per cup.
Let x be the number cups of Super Grain cereal in one cup of mixture. Thus, we can write the equation to solve for x as follows:
\begin{align*}
&\text{Calories from Crunchy Grain cereal} + \text{Calories from Super Grain cereal} = \text{Total Calories} \\
&\frac{210}{\frac{3}{4}} + \frac{240}{1} \times x = 270 \times 1 \\
&280 + 240x = 270 \\
&240x = 270 - 280 \\
&240x = -10 \\
&x = \boxed{\textbf{(A)} \:\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}}
\end{align*}

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$The equation above gives the height $h$, in feet, of a ball $t$ seconds after it is thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet. Which of the following gives $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: $v=h+k-16 t$
  B: $v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}$
  C: $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$
  D: $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16 t$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
We are given that 
    $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$ and we want to solve for $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$
  
Action: 
First, isolate $v$ on one side of the equation, by adding $- k$ and $+16 t^2$ to each side, so we get:
  $$ h -k + 16t^2 = -16t^2 + vt + k + 16t^2$$
Simplify by canceling out the $k$ and $16t^2:$
  $$h - k + 16t^2 = vt$$
Divide both sides by $t$ to solve for $v:$
  $$v = \frac{h - k + 16t^2}{t}$$
  which simplifies to:
  $$v = \frac{h - k}{t} +16t$$
  
Therefore, the answer is (D) $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16t$.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
We are given the height function of a ball thrown straight up as $$h=-16t^{2}+vt+k$$
We are asked to solve for $v$ in terms of $h,$ $t$ and $k.$

Solution:
First, we isolate the $v$ term to one side of the equation by subtracting $k$ from both sides, which gives $$h-k=-16t^{2}+vt$$
Next, we divide both sides by $t,$ which gives $$\frac{h-k}{t}=-16t+v$$
Finally, we add $16t$ to both sides, which gives $$v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16t$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\mathrm{(D)}\ v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16t}$.

$$v = 16t^2 + h - k$$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$-2 x+3 y=6$$In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is perpendicular to the graph of the equation above?
Choices:
  A: $3 x+2 y=6$
  B: $3 x+4 y=6$
  C: $2 x+4 y=6$
  D: $2 x+6 y=3$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
Two lines are perpendicular if and only if the product of their slopes is -1.
To put the equation of the line in slope-intercept form, we can solve for $y$.

$$-2 x+3 y=6 \Rightarrow 3y = 2x + 6 \Rightarrow y = \frac{2}{3}x + 2 $$

A: To convert $3 x+2 y=6$ to slope-intercept form, we solve for $y$.  
   $$2 y = -3 x + 6 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{3}{2} x + 3$$
   
   The slope of the line $y=-\frac{3}{2}x+3$ is $-\frac{3}{2}$. Therefore, the product of the slopes of the two lines is 
   
   $$\left(-\frac{3}{2}\right)\left(\frac{2}{3}\right) = -1$$
   
   So the line $3 x+2 y=6$ is perpendicular to the line $y = -\frac{3}{2} x + 3$. But this is not the answer to the question, which asks for a line whose graph is perpendicular to the line $-2x+3y=6$.
   
B: To convert $3 x+4 y=6$ to slope-intercept form, we solve for $y$.  
   $$4 y = -3 x + 6 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{3}{4} x + \frac{3}{4}$$
   
   The slope of the line $y=-\frac{3}{4}x+\frac{3}{4}$ is $-\frac{3}{4}$. Therefore, the product of the slopes of the two lines is 
   
   $$\left(-\frac{3}{4}\right)\left(\frac{2}{3}\right) = -\frac{1}{2}$$
   
   So the line $3 x+4 y=6$ is not perpendicular to the line $-2x+3y=6$.
   
C: To convert $2 x+4 y=6$ to slope-intercept form, we solve for $y$.  
   $$4 y = -2 x + 6 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{1}{2} x + \frac{3}{2}$$
   
   The slope of the line $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{3}{2}$ is $-\frac{1}{2}$. Therefore, the product of the slopes of the two lines is 
   
   $$\left(-\frac{1}{2}\right)\left(\frac{2}{3}\right) = -\frac{1}{3}$$
   
   So the line $2 x+4 y=6$ is not perpendicular to the line $-2x+3y=6$.
   
D: To convert $2 x+6 y=3$ to slope-intercept form, we solve for $y$.  
   $$6 y = -2 x + 3 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{1}{3} x + \frac{1}{2}$$
   
   The slope of the line $y=-\frac{1}{3}x+\frac{1}{2}$ is $-\frac{1}{3}$. Therefore, the product of the slopes of the two lines is 
   
   $$\left(-\frac{1}{3}\right)\left(\frac{2}{3}\right) = -\frac{2}{9}$$
   
   So the line $2 x+6 y=3$ is not perpendicular to the line $-2x+3y=6$.
   
Action: Answer("A")

Question: Biologists found a new species of pale shrimp at the world's deepest undersea vent, the Beebe Vent Field. The vent is 3.1 miles below the sea's surface.Approximately how many kilometers below the sea's surface is the vent? ( 1 kilometer $\approx 0.6214$ miles)
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The Beebe Vent Field is 3.1 miles below the sea's surface.
  1 kilometer $\approx 0.6214$ miles, which means that 1 mile $\approx 1/0.6214$ or approximately 1.609 kilometers.
Action: We can find out how many kilometers below the sea's surface the vent is by dividing the depth in miles by the conversion factor from miles to kilometers. That is: $3.1\text{ miles}\div 1.609\approx 1.93\text{ kilometers}.$
Therefore, the answer is not one of the given choices, and the most appropriate choice is A: 2.

Knowledge:
  1 kilometer is approximately 0.6214 miles.
  The Beebe Vent Field is 3.1 miles below the sea's surface.
  We can use multiplication/division to convert miles to kilometers.
Calculation: 
  3.1 miles * (1 kilometer/0.6214 miles) = 4.988 kilometers

Topic: Math
Question: The Downtown Business Association (DBA) in a certain city plans to increase its membership by a total of $n$ businesses per year. There were $b$ businesses in the DBA at the beginning of this year. Which function best models the total number of businesses, $y$, the DBA plans to have as members $x$ years from now?

  A: $y=n x+b$
  B: $y=n x-b$
  C: $y=b(n)^{x}$
  D: $y=n(b)^{x}$

Question: $$\frac{x}{x-3}=\frac{2 x}{2}$$Which of the following represents all the possible values of $x$ that satisfy the equation above?
Choices:
  A: 0 and 2
  B: 0 and 4
  C: -4 and 4
  D: 4
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To solve this equation, we can cross multiply and simplify.
  $$\frac{x}{x-3}=\frac{2 x}{2} \Rightarrow x(x-3)=2x  \Rightarrow x^{2}-5x=0 \Rightarrow x(x-5)=0$$ 
  Therefore, we have two possible solutions: $x=0$ and $x=5$.
  A: 0 and 2 are not both solutions of the equation.
  B: 0 and 4 are not both solutions of the equation.
  C: -4 is not a solution of the equation, while 4 is a solution, but it is not the only one.
  D: 4 is a solution of the equation, but it is not the only one.
Action: Answer("E")   (None of the above)
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We can start by cross multiplying each side of the equation and then simplifying to find the values of x that satisfy the equation.
  \begin{align*}
  \frac{x}{x-3} &= \frac{2 x}{2}\\
  \Rightarrow 2x(x-3) &= (x)(2)\\
  \Rightarrow 2x^2-6x &= 2x\\
  \Rightarrow 2x^2-8x &= 0\\
  \Rightarrow 2x(x-4) &= 0\\
  \end{align*}
  Using the zero product property, we get $x=0$ or $x-4=0$, which gives us $x=4$.

Action: Answer("B") - 0 and 4.

$$x^2 - 4x = 0$$
$$x(x-4) = 0$$
$$x = 0, 4$$

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Knowledge: To solve the system of equations above, one can use elimination or substitution method. However, we are looking for the value of k for which the system of equations has no solution. This occurs when the lines represented by the equations are parallel. Two lines are parallel if and only if their slopes are equal and their y-intercepts are different.
Action: 
Rearrange the first equation to get $kx=3y+4$, which implies $x=\frac{3}{k}y+\frac{4}{k}$. The slope of this line is $\frac{3}{k}$.
The slope of the second line is $\frac{4}{5}$.
For the lines to be parallel, we must have: $\frac{3}{k}=\frac{4}{5}$. This gives $k=\frac{15}{4}$.
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ \frac{12}{5}}$.

Action: 
We can solve this system of equations using any preferred method such as elimination, substitution, graphing, matrix, or determinant methods. Here, we will use the elimination method to remove $y$ and solve for $x$:
\begin{align*}

kx-3y&=4\\
3(4x-5y)&=3\cdot 7 &\text{(from the second equation)} \\

\end{align*}

25kx-15y&=20\\
3(12x-15y)&=3\cdot 21\\

\end{align*}

25kx-15y&=20\\
-&(25x-45y=63)\\ \hline
&(25k-25)x=-43
\end{align*}

-\frac{43k}{25k-25}-3y&=4\\
-\frac{43k+12(25k-25)}{25k-25}&=y\\
y&=-\frac{43k+300}{25k-25}
\end{align*}
Therefore, the system has no solution when the denominator in the equation for $y$ is $0$. That is, when $25k-25=0$, or $k=\boxed{\textbf{(D)} -\frac{12}{5}}$.
Response 9:
Knowledge: To solve a system of linear equations, we can use elimination method or substitution method. If we get a contradiction like $0=1$, then the system has no solutions.  
Solution: 

We can solve this system by multiplying the first equation by $5$ and the second equation by $3$, then add the two equations to eliminate $y$.

$$\begin{aligned}& 5 k x-15 y=20 \\& 12 x-15 y=21\end{aligned}$$

Subtracting the second equation from the first one, we have:

$$5 k x-12 x=20-21$$
$$(5k-12)x=-1$$

Thus, we have:

$$x=\frac{-1}{5k-12}$$

Now we substitute $x$ into one of the equations to get $y$. Using the first equation:

$$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\ \Rightarrow & k \cdot \frac{-1}{5k-12}-3 y=4\end{aligned}$$

Simplifying, we get:

$$y = \frac{5k-16}{3(5k-12)}$$

So the system has no solution if $x$ is undefined (which means $5k-12=0$) and $y$ has a value (which means $5k-16 \neq 0$). Therefore, we must have:

$$5k-12=0$$
$$k=\frac{12}{5}$$

Thus, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ \frac{12}{5}}$.

Response 5:
Knowledge:
We can solve the given equation for $b/a$ by cross-multiplying. We have:

$$
\frac{2a}{b} = \frac{1}{2}
$$

Cross-multiplying both sides of the equation by $b$ gives:

$$
2a = \frac{b}{2} = \frac{1}{2}b
$$

Cross-multiplying both sides of this equation by 2 gives:

$$
4a = b
$$

Therefore, $\frac{b}{a} = 4/a$.
